    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText13256595822062344332" style="display:none"><b>There is an unseen world of good and evil where nightmares are fought and hope is reborn. Enter <i>The Door Within.</i></b><br /><br />Aidan Thomas is miserable. Within two weeks, Aidan’s life is completely uprooted as his parents move the family across the country to care for his ailing grandfather. The quiet but imaginative Aidan is struggling with attending a new school and fitting in with a new group of friends. But when he begins having nightmares and eerie events occur around his neighborhood, Aidan finds himself drawn to his grandfather's basement—where he discovers three ancient scrolls and a mysterious invitation to another world.<br /><br />No longer confined to the realm of his own imagination, Aidan embarks on an adventure where he discovers a long-fought war between good and evil. With the fate of two worlds hanging in the balance, Aidan faces Paragory, the eternal enemy with unfathomable power. Will Aidan be willing to risk everything and trust the unseen hand of the one true King?</span>

The fire rain had been unleashed."<br /><br />As Cat's memory returns, he realizes that he has lived two very different lives: One as the son of the ruthless Bartholomew Thorne; the other as the recipient of friendship and kindness from Declan Ross and the crew of the Robert Bruce. Now Cat must choose whether to return to the ways of his notorious father and join the evil Merchant, or defy the Merchant and risk his life to save his friends.<br /><br />The best-selling Isle of Swords adventure continues in Isle of Fire as ancient mariners rise from legend and cut an all-too-real swath of destruction across the Atlantic. The newly formed Wolf Fleet scours the Caribbean, hunting the pirates they once called comrades. <div id="review_79143219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79143219" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2911115-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79143219?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/2911115-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2911115-hannah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79143219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5917225244546263080">Okay. No offense to the author, but this book was not as good as it could have been. I love Christian fiction as a rule, but this was...well, it wasn't Tolkien-Lewis standard. The symbolism was a little heavy. No, that was a lie. It was akin to being thwacked over the head with a hard-cover Bible. In my mind, there are two pieces of advice that every allegory writer must have:<br/>A) Plot (and writing!) that's good quality separate from the Biblical references. Case in point: The Chronicles of Narnia</span>
  <span id="freeText5917225244546263080" style="display:none">Okay. No offense to the author, but this book was not as good as it could have been. I love Christian fiction as a rule, but this was...well, it wasn't Tolkien-Lewis standard. The symbolism was a little heavy. No, that was a lie. It was akin to being thwacked over the head with a hard-cover Bible. In my mind, there are two pieces of advice that every allegory writer must have:<br />A) Plot (and writing!) that's good quality separate from the Biblical references. Case in point: The Chronicles of Narnia. If you aren't Christian, you can read the books with enjoyment. If the only redeeming feature of your book is the Christian allegory, you've got a problem. <br />B)Be subtle! If you have a symbol in your text, you don't have to change your tone completely to point it out. If someone doesn't get it, that's okay. If they do note the symbol, that's good. But we're going for subliminal, here.<br />The Door Within Trilogy (again, no offense meant, and I'm trying to be tactful)has neither of these. It's more likely to scare off non-Christians than draw them in. It almost scared <i>me</i> off. So my suggestion is: worry less about everybody getting the symbols and worry more about writing a book that people will enjoy.<br />This review is pretty much the same for all the books in this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5917225244546263080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41747361-c-b-cook?shelf=own">own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1265769222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16986706384224159737">Well. Wow. I thought I would like this book, but I didn't expect to enjoy it that much! Sure, it doesn't beat books like <i>Lord of the Rings</i> or <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i>, but it was really enjoyable! If I had to describe this book as if it were a person, I would say it was perky, fun, and intriguing.<br/><br/><b>The Good</b><br/>There were soooo many unique ideas in this story! Fantasy books can have a lot of clichés, and of course this one has some, but there are plenty of unique ideas that help offset that. Moonrascal</span>
  <span id="freeText16986706384224159737" style="display:none">Well. Wow. I thought I would like this book, but I didn't expect to enjoy it that much! Sure, it doesn't beat books like <i>Lord of the Rings</i> or <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i>, but it was really enjoyable! If I had to describe this book as if it were a person, I would say it was perky, fun, and intriguing.<br /><br /><b>The Good</b><br />There were soooo many unique ideas in this story! Fantasy books can have a lot of clichés, and of course this one has some, but there are plenty of unique ideas that help offset that. Moonrascals are awesome (can I please have one?), Falon was AMAZINGLY AWESOME (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She can make herself look like a glittering maze? That's just plain <i>cool</i>! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), and I loved the idea of Glimpses. Lantern spiders, mortiwraith poison... I felt like there was a lot in this story that I hadn't seen before. <br /><br />The world and the characters were really intriguing, too. Eyes flashing colors, Mallik with his Mjolnir-like hammer, Bolt and Nock... Captain Valithor was really cool, as were many of the other characters.<br /><br />I loved how funny this book was! It was tense, but light, mostly because it's middle grade-ish instead of YA. It was a great relief from a lot of those fantasy books that are more focused on world and fighting and suspense and death and romance and such. <br /><br /><b>The Bad</b><br />Some of the characters could have used a little more development, and a few places were pretty predictable. But if you're look for a light, fun read, this is it. <br /><br /><b>The Ugly</b><br />Nothing truly bad here, mostly minor violence. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Several characters we love die. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, I really, really enjoyed this book, and had fun reading it. Now, if you'll excuse me, I must go read Winter. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16986706384224159737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10418788420109798562">Upset with his family’s sudden move across the country, Aidan Thomas is friendless and bored. He seeks out adventure by exploring his new home which takes him to the dark and creepy basement. He finds dusty boxes of old toys, stacks of newspapers from the 1950s, and an old radio. It all seems to be a typical basement until a blue light grows out of the darkness leaving three clay pots in its wake.   <span id="freeText10418788420109798562" style="display:none">Upset with his family’s sudden move across the country, Aidan Thomas is friendless and bored. He seeks out adventure by exploring his new home which takes him to the dark and creepy basement. He finds dusty boxes of old toys, stacks of newspapers from the 1950s, and an old radio. It all seems to be a typical basement until a blue light grows out of the darkness leaving three clay pots in its wake. Inside them, Aidan finds three ancient scrolls.<br /><br />He takes his newfound treasure to his room and begins to read a story about a knight who betrayed his king. He also reads a poem that ends: Believe and enter. Achan tries to talk to his parents about his discovery, but they’re too busy at first, then they don’t believe him, assuring their son it is nothing but a story. But Aidan’s grandfather believes and encourages Aidan to trust in his own heart. That night, Aidan reads the poem again, decides to believe, and enters The Door Within.<br /><br />He is whisked into a medieval land of dragons, knights, and castles and discovers that the kingdom is in danger. A group of knights are getting ready to travel to Mitheguard, a city that has not yet taken a side in the battle for good and evil. They’ve only been waiting for the king to choose a twelfth knight, and Aidan is informed that the king has. Aidan.<br /><br />The Door Within is a fun allegorical tale that takes a regular kid into a medieval world where good and evil are struggling to win the faith of a kingdom, one soul at a time. I enjoyed the way Wayne Thomas Batson connected the real world with The Realm inside the door. Very creative and fun. Two thumbs up. Recommended.<br /></span>

<div id="review_92359689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92359689" />
    <a title="Molly Evangeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3376321-molly-evangeline"><img alt="Molly Evangeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380312236p2/3376321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92359689?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly Evangeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly Evangeline" href="/user/show/3376321-molly-evangeline">Molly Evangeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3376321-molly-evangeline?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92359689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12290634745773071793">When I first found out about The Door Within Trilogy while I was working at the local bookstore a couple years ago, I have to admit, it didn't grab my attention. For some odd reason, which I can't even recall now, I thought it might be a little too juvenile for me. Boy, I don't think I'll ever judge a book so quickly again. Being the Christian fantasy fan that I am, I finally got the books from the library and from page one I was completely hooked. The entire trilogy had me reading almost non-st</span>
  <span id="freeText12290634745773071793" style="display:none">When I first found out about The Door Within Trilogy while I was working at the local bookstore a couple years ago, I have to admit, it didn't grab my attention. For some odd reason, which I can't even recall now, I thought it might be a little too juvenile for me. Boy, I don't think I'll ever judge a book so quickly again. Being the Christian fantasy fan that I am, I finally got the books from the library and from page one I was completely hooked. The entire trilogy had me reading almost non-stop and when I'd finished, I had to buy my own set to read again. I don't think any fiction series has impacted me like The Door Within. I read the trilogy to my youngest brother who is not a big fan of fiction. In the beginning, I more or less forced him to sit down and listen, but soon he was coming to me, begging me to read more. Even now, months later, he still talks to me about different scenes in the book. Like me, he was deeply affected by the story. <br /><br />One of my favorite aspects of the trilogy is the characters and their growth. They are so endearing and diverse, and you really feel for them and their struggles. The allegorical and spiritual parts of the books are amazing. Once you finish, you have a deep sense of longing to be a knight for the one true King, to stand firm in what is right no matter the cost, and grow in your faith. The books are a wonderful example of friendship, sacrifice, faith, and growth. There is also a perfect amount of humor that had me and my brother laughing out loud numerous times. I recommend The Door Within to anyone of any age who enjoys a good adventure story with a great message woven in. And they are excellent read aloud books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12290634745773071793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_186690457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186690457" />
    <a title="Adam Ross" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1919392-adam-ross"><img alt="Adam Ross" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241219328p2/1919392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186690457?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Ross" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Ross" href="/user/show/1919392-adam-ross">Adam Ross</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1919392-adam-ross?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186690457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12827450251584275811">I wanted to like this book. I did. Unfortunately, I thought it continued to illustrate the problems with the Christian fiction publishing industry. It was not so much the story I had a problem with, but the prose was less than stellar, and the character development wasn't up to snuff. Repeatedly I found myself puzzled by character decisions that seemed to make no sense. I didn't get the wonder I was obviously supposed to get by having a boy stumble into a magical world. Nothing actually happens </span>
  <span id="freeText12827450251584275811" style="display:none">I wanted to like this book. I did. Unfortunately, I thought it continued to illustrate the problems with the Christian fiction publishing industry. It was not so much the story I had a problem with, but the prose was less than stellar, and the character development wasn't up to snuff. Repeatedly I found myself puzzled by character decisions that seemed to make no sense. I didn't get the wonder I was obviously supposed to get by having a boy stumble into a magical world. Nothing actually happens in the first hundred pages and Batson breaks the cardinal rule of fiction, which is: don't info-dump your backstory. Yet we're treated to the entire backstory in two entire chapters in a row where the author is literally telling us everything that happened. Big no-no. So I missed the wonder of this book; but I wish I hadn't. As I say, I really wanted to like this book. Younger kids will probably enjoy it anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12827450251584275811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_53905535" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53905535" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256262-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442983573p2/1256262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53905535?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/1256262-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256262-ron?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256262-ron?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256262-ron?shelf=young">young</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53905535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer440794069536209597">Derived. "Revenge of the Nerds" meets "The Hobbit."<br/><br/>A good if hardly original concept, but Batson should have worked harder (though he claims it took him thirteen years) making it his own work. Reads like a dashed off ripoff of Christian classic fantasy with too much Narnia, Middle Earth overlap.<br/><br/>Reminds you why J. R. R. Tolkien hated allegory. Speaking of whom, Tolkien would be angered (as he was with C. S. Lewis) at the way Batson misused mythology. Specifically, the insertion of unicorns as hor</span>
  <span id="freeText440794069536209597" style="display:none">Derived. "Revenge of the Nerds" meets "The Hobbit."<br /><br />A good if hardly original concept, but Batson should have worked harder (though he claims it took him thirteen years) making it his own work. Reads like a dashed off ripoff of Christian classic fantasy with too much Narnia, Middle Earth overlap.<br /><br />Reminds you why J. R. R. Tolkien hated allegory. Speaking of whom, Tolkien would be angered (as he was with C. S. Lewis) at the way Batson misused mythology. Specifically, the insertion of unicorns as horse substitutes just to give the story an "other" flavor but without regard to the history and mythology of unicorns is exactly what drove Tolkien up the wall about Lewis's sloppy mixing and matching of myths in Narnia. And Batson is no Lewis. (To learn more, read Tolkein's "On Fairy-Stories" in <i>The Tolkien Reader</i>.<br /><br />Having his short, pudgy hero transformed into a sword-wielding hero in a week pushes even the credibility of the teen nerds who seem to be the target audience.<br /><br />Batson researched Medieval technology and terminology but seems unaware of his gaffs in time and travel (is that why he substituted unicorns for the horses who would have died attempting the travel feats chronicled?), not to mention having too dense a population in too small a world.<br /><br />Not sure I'd read the follow-on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="440794069536209597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1283368187" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283368187" />
    <a title="Ashley Bogner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43202587-ashley-bogner"><img alt="Ashley Bogner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549942031p2/43202587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283368187?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Bogner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Bogner" href="/user/show/43202587-ashley-bogner">Ashley Bogner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43202587-ashley-bogner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283368187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18292645467738459262">Several years ago, a friend recommended <i> The Door Within </i> to me. I decided to pick it up at the library, and was smart enough to get the consecutive books as well. From the first chapter, I was hooked. I read the entire trilogy in a few days and couldn’t put the series down. Since then, I’ve read several of Wayne Thomas Batson’s other books and loved them.<br/><br/>In <i> The Door Within </i>, teenager Aidan Thomas is frustrated with his parent’s decision to move the family halfway across the country. He misses </span>
  <span id="freeText18292645467738459262" style="display:none">Several years ago, a friend recommended <i> The Door Within </i> to me. I decided to pick it up at the library, and was smart enough to get the consecutive books as well. From the first chapter, I was hooked. I read the entire trilogy in a few days and couldn’t put the series down. Since then, I’ve read several of Wayne Thomas Batson’s other books and loved them.<br /><br />In <i> The Door Within </i>, teenager Aidan Thomas is frustrated with his parent’s decision to move the family halfway across the country. He misses his best friend and isn’t exactly thrilled to be living with his crazy grandfather. Soon Aidan finds an ancient scroll in his grandfather’s basement…and finds himself transported to a magical world filled with knights, dragons, and castles. Oh, yeah, and a power-hungry man with ambitions to take over the kingdom.<br /><br /><i> The Door Within </i> is just plain ol’ fun to read. It’s a great mix of adventure, sword fights, betrayal, friendship, suspense, and comic relief. Sure, the silly antics and witty banter can feel a bit cheesy at times, but in a good way.<br /><br />But beneath the action and humor lies spiritual truth. <i> The Door Within </i> is an allegory in the same vein as C.S. Lewis’ <i> The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe </i> (one of my all-time favorite books). I love how the book reminds us to have faith even we can’t see God and it’s hard to know for certain He’s there. The characters frequently remind each other that when it seems like the battle can’t be won, they’re “never alone”.<br /><br />I love that reminder.<br /><br />I’ve read the entire trilogy multiple times, and I highly recommend it to anyone who loves allegorical fantasy or just a fun, imaginative adventure. Oh–and it’s also one of those rare cases where each book is even better than the last.<br /><br />(Review originally found on my blog)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18292645467738459262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_874006665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/874006665" />
    <a title="Michael O&#39;Brien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9496879-michael-o-brien"><img alt="Michael O&#39;Brien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548207742p2/9496879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/874006665?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael O&#39;Brien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael O&#39;Brien" href="/user/show/9496879-michael-o-brien">Michael O&#39;Brien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer874006665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18263790447455893862">Saw this trilogy recommended by a friend on Facebook, and it struck my interest. It was very readable, and could be enjoyed by both adults and children at a sixth grade reading level and above. It's Christian fantasy, comparable to the Chronicles of Narnia, and is also an allegory of the battle between God's forces and those of darkness, and the struggle for those who have not decided --- in some ways it reminded me of "Pilgrim's Progress". Looking forward to reading the next book in the series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10183256585581005525">A lot of folks seem to really like this, but I...really don't. It's pretty predictable, nothing's very well developed (including the main character, which is a big no-no in my view), the Christian imagery is so overt as to be distracting, the writing feels dumbed down, and...well, I guess that's it. In the end I found I just didn't care. I will certainly not be reading the rest of the books in this series.</span>

<div id="review_720507454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/720507454" />
    <a title="Jacob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/901342-jacob"><img alt="Jacob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555491633p2/901342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/720507454?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob" href="/user/show/901342-jacob">Jacob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=from_library">from_library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=youth">youth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer720507454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2858547100981182483">I don't exactly remember adding this to my to-read list a couple of years ago, but it wasn't the hidden gem I thought it might turn out as. The writing is stilted and overwrought and the story is kind of clumsy. I know this is targeted towards youth but other series like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60400.The_Ruins_of_Gorlan__Ranger_s_Apprentice___1_' title='The Ruins of Gorlan (Ranger's Apprentice, #1) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Ruins of Gorlan</a> or books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story' title='The Neverending Story by Michael Ende' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Neverending Story</a> are targeted the same way and better written. I don't know why it is this way; the edition I read included "lost chapters" at the end, which were a set of longer original b</span>
  <span id="freeText2858547100981182483" style="display:none">I don't exactly remember adding this to my to-read list a couple of years ago, but it wasn't the hidden gem I thought it might turn out as. The writing is stilted and overwrought and the story is kind of clumsy. I know this is targeted towards youth but other series like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60400.The_Ruins_of_Gorlan__Ranger_s_Apprentice___1_" title="The Ruins of Gorlan (Ranger's Apprentice, #1) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ruins of Gorlan</a> or books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27712.The_Neverending_Story" title="The Neverending Story by Michael Ende" rel="nofollow noopener">The Neverending Story</a> are targeted the same way and better written. I don't know why it is this way; the edition I read included "lost chapters" at the end, which were a set of longer original beginning chapters the author had to condense. Normally that kind of editing makes the writing better, especially in the beginning which a lot of authors handle awkwardly, but it seems in this case it didn't. So this book doesn't work exceptionally well as a story, especially since so many things seem to just happen arbitrarily.<br /><br />The smoothness and believable causality of the story flow may have been a casualty of the author's deliberately making this allegorical. I didn't realize when I started the book that it was intentionally Christian allegory, but you can't really miss it. It becomes painfully obvious even before the character Rucifel shows up. I really think allegory is much better when it happens naturally and bubbles up through an author's subconscious into something which becomes obvious only in retrospect (like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7236997.The_Native_Star__Veneficas_Americana___1_" title="The Native Star (Veneficas Americana, #1) by M.K. Hobson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Native Star</a> and its oil, er, whatever-you-call-it).<br /><br />So, to sum up: not the worst thing I've ever read, and your kids might enjoy it if they were hard up for better material, but generally not worth the time.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2858547100981182483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Whisper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2914078-whisper"><img alt="Whisper" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76960820?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whisper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whisper" href="/user/show/2914078-whisper">Whisper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76960820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3150831287199277966">Wow. This book is great. Enough battles and peril to satisfy the adventure-lover, enough secrets to satisfy the mystery-lover, and enough coolness to satisfy the... well, cool-lover!<br/><br/>All around great. Granted, some might see it as "just another fantasy book", but it most certainly has characteristics that distinguish it from others in its genre.<br/><br/>For instance, there is an unlikely connection between Earth and The Realm... but I won't spoil that for you. :-D Also, there is a good dose of Biblical al</span>
  <span id="freeText3150831287199277966" style="display:none">Wow. This book is great. Enough battles and peril to satisfy the adventure-lover, enough secrets to satisfy the mystery-lover, and enough coolness to satisfy the... well, cool-lover!<br /><br />All around great. Granted, some might see it as "just another fantasy book", but it most certainly has characteristics that distinguish it from others in its genre.<br /><br />For instance, there is an unlikely connection between Earth and The Realm... but I won't spoil that for you. :-D Also, there is a good dose of Biblical allegory, enough to inspire and appeal to Christian readers, yet not so much that the books would be termed "preachy" by most non-Christians. It would still be a marvelous book even without these themes.<br /><br />This is also a welcome addition to the book world because, by almost all standards, it is clean. I have tried many other fantasy tales and been sorely disappointed by inappropriate words and references.<br /><br />This book is emotional, as well. Beloved characters die, yet even in those times, there is hope...<br /><br />I will mention that its main downside would be, in my opinion, the fact that there were a grammar issues that I found distracting. Nonetheless, I enjoyed the plot and characters so much that I still am giving this book all five stars.<br /><br />Dragons, knights, sieges, tornadoes, mazes, traitors and lantern spiders. Find all this and more... if you choose to enter the door within.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3150831287199277966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2044146241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2044146241" />
    <a title="Karissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa"><img alt="Karissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557318686p2/4057501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2044146241?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karissa" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa">Karissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2044146241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3593151966492026603">I got this book quite a while ago when I was looking for some good middle grade fantasy adventure to read and saw the very high reviews for this trilogy. This was not a book for me. For those who aren’t aware (as I was not) Batson is a Christian author who publishes books with strong Christian themes to them. In general I don’t have issue with that but this book was incredibly poorly written and written at a very basic reading level (short sentences and simple words). It’s like it was written fo</span>
  <span id="freeText3593151966492026603" style="display:none">I got this book quite a while ago when I was looking for some good middle grade fantasy adventure to read and saw the very high reviews for this trilogy. This was not a book for me. For those who aren’t aware (as I was not) Batson is a Christian author who publishes books with strong Christian themes to them. In general I don’t have issue with that but this book was incredibly poorly written and written at a very basic reading level (short sentences and simple words). It’s like it was written for small children but then deals with the subject of war, evil, and faith. It’s too violent for small children and too simply written for middle grade readers.<br /> <br />When I started the book I thought it was okay. There’s some creative ideas in here but in general it’s a pretty basic and overdone story for the fantasy genre. The plot was this...unhappy boy finds a way into a fantasy world where he becomes a great knight and saves the day. Then suddenly finds himself back home but is a better person for his adventures. Yawn….read that plot a million times before.<br /> <br />The difference is that in the magical world of Alleble Aiden becomes a Knight to the one true King (do you smell religion here?). The one true King will provide for his followers in times of need even though he has no clear form. He also values kindness over violence and if you (for example) lay down your sword in front of an enemy instead of attack them everything will go your way because the one true King is all knowing and sees you and helps you. There is a lot of preachiness about faith in the one true power throughout the book which always bothers me because it allows characters to fall back on The King and his power rather than allow them to empower themselves.<br /> <br />Okay preachiness aside let’s talk Aiden’s character for a second. Aiden is an incredibly whiny and selfish middle aged child. His parents move to help take care of his ailing Grandpa and all he can do is whine and complain. Yes, kids complain but in general if raised properly kids are also smart, helpful, and caring...they are not one dimensional people. I don’t know how Aiden’s parents managed to raise such a selfish brat, but my 10 year old son is a lot more understanding and helpful than Aiden ever is. In fact most kids I have dealt with are.<br /> <br />Okay next the story. When Aiden gets to Alleble he is immediately in trouble only to be saved by cute fuzzy creatures and a dragon; I was down with that, it’s a fun start to the story. Then he ends up joining with the King’s Knights and starts his training as a knight because The King knows Aiden is destined for great things. Within a week Aiden (who is described as overweight, out of shape and lazy earlier in the book) is able to best some of the grown-up knights with his sword skill. Ummm….what? That makes no sense. Way to show kids that you can be lazy slobs and then if The King believes in you you suddenly become a kick-butt hero...I guess it is a fantasy.<br /> <br />The story pretty much goes downhill from there. There is a woman knight named Gwenne, who of course is the only knight to be kidnapped and in need of rescue after her womanly tenderness gets her caught by the enemy while rescuing a child. She was the only woman character in the whole book. Definitely no good female role models here….<br /> <br />Overall this was an absolutely awful book. From the overly simplistic jerky writing and the predictable plot to the preachy tones and poor excuse for a hero. Faith is overly preached and there are no good adult or female role models. It was a awful struggle me to finish this very basic easy-to-read book. This is awful. I would recommend staying far away from this book. <br /> <br />If you are looking for an amazing middle grade fantasy check out the Harry Potter series, the Percy Jackson series, the Ranger’s Apprentice series, the Unwanteds series, the Map to Everywhere series, the Wings of Fire series, the Saavy series, the Magesterium series, or any number of wonderful Middle Grade fantasy series out there.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3593151966492026603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1084156745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16521912925867951323">The book “The Door Within” was an outstanding book. The book starts off with a teenage boy named Aiden Thomas who is the short, plump, and unpopular. Everything changes for Aidan when his grandpa becomes sick because his family has to move to Colorado to take care of him. Aidan is miserable because he misses his friends, is lonely, and bored trying to find something to do. He decides to explore his grandpa's basement. He finds three old scrolls that tell a story of two kingdoms, Alleble and Para</span>
  <span id="freeText16521912925867951323" style="display:none">The book “The Door Within” was an outstanding book. The book starts off with a teenage boy named Aiden Thomas who is the short, plump, and unpopular. Everything changes for Aidan when his grandpa becomes sick because his family has to move to Colorado to take care of him. Aidan is miserable because he misses his friends, is lonely, and bored trying to find something to do. He decides to explore his grandpa's basement. He finds three old scrolls that tell a story of two kingdoms, Alleble and Paragory. Paragory was named after its evil ruler Paragor. Paragor has attacked Alleble and is fighting to get rule over The Realm. The story sounds so real to Aiden that he begins to think that The Realm and the kingdoms do exist. Aiden tells his father, but he doesn’t believe the scrolls and calls them myths, however, his grandpa says that the kingdoms are real, and believing in it will open a door to The Realm. As Aidan reads the scroll’s last line which says,” Believe and enter”, he gets into Alleble. Once he’s in Alleble he decides that he will follow the King of Alleble, but not Paragor because he is mischievous. The King of Alleble chooses Aiden to become a part of a special group of warriors who defend the land of Alleble. Aidan is trained by Captain Valithor and is told to go to the kingdom of Mithegard and persuade there king not to form an alliance with Paragor.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16521912925867951323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_124675860" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124675860" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4269230-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300191814p2/4269230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124675860?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/4269230-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269230-michelle?shelf=bad-theological-implications">bad-theological-implications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4269230-michelle?shelf=bland-protagonist">bland-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124675860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10650501838304297306"> The Door Within is pretty typical Christian Fantasy, though well-written and with some original ideas. Boy finds link to fantasy world and goes through and saves the day--temporarily, this being part of a series. New is the idea that this world is a sort of alternate universe, with everyone having an albino duplicate.<br/> This book falls prey to two chestnuts of Christian writing: overly large and shallow cast, and the roles of good and evil.<br/> The expected Christ figure is decent, though typical. A </span>
  <span id="freeText10650501838304297306" style="display:none"> The Door Within is pretty typical Christian Fantasy, though well-written and with some original ideas. Boy finds link to fantasy world and goes through and saves the day--temporarily, this being part of a series. New is the idea that this world is a sort of alternate universe, with everyone having an albino duplicate.<br /> This book falls prey to two chestnuts of Christian writing: overly large and shallow cast, and the roles of good and evil.<br /> The expected Christ figure is decent, though typical. A standard I have noticed in Christian books is that people are one of three orientations: good, evil and future convert. There is also a theme in any fantasy book about being able to tell a person's level of goodness or even simple emotions by their eyes. These two cliches meet again here, with characters having blue, red or green eyes depending on where they stand.<br /> Why don't writers ever learn? We don't need fifty people involved to know this is a serious conflict, just pick a few and develop them so we can remember who you're talking about! If you need to include a "who's who," you have too many people.<br /> In summary, Wayne Thomas Batson is a fine writer, he just doesn't have anything new to say here. I recommend his pirate books for more originality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10650501838304297306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704972808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17364756278032853929"> It’s utterly fascinating how every fantasy series I read is so completely different from the next. There are so many varied takes on Christian allegories/fantasies, I don’t think I’ll ever tire of this genre! <br/> <br/> <i>The Door Within</i> was even better than I imagined! –A fantastic tale! My mind is whirling with the in-depth storyline, and the new concepts introduced in this fantasy. I totally fell in love with Aiden’s story, and the Glimpses, and the whole adventure! I must admit though, the serpent-li</span>
  <span id="freeText17364756278032853929" style="display:none"> It’s utterly fascinating how every fantasy series I read is so completely different from the next. There are so many varied takes on Christian allegories/fantasies, I don’t think I’ll ever tire of this genre! <br /> <br /> <i>The Door Within</i> was even better than I imagined! –A fantastic tale! My mind is whirling with the in-depth storyline, and the new concepts introduced in this fantasy. I totally fell in love with Aiden’s story, and the Glimpses, and the whole adventure! I must admit though, the serpent-like creature named Falon, grossed me out a little… if you know anything about me… yeah, I don’t prefer things like that. However, the overall story made up for that. Totally different. Totally fresh and new. Though kind of in the tradition of <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i>, what with a secret, fantasy world amidst our own.<br /> <br /> The Door Within series can be for a wide range of ages. I thoroughly enjoyed it, and I think my little siblings would enjoy it too… eleven and thirteen.<br /> <br /> This was just an incredible story… I’m so shocked… and then fascinated… and I can’t wait for <i>The Rise of the Wyrm Lord</i>!!</span>

<div id="review_2906925629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2906925629" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9499718-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551817464p2/9499718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2906925629?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/9499718-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781400306596" href="/book/show/905196.The_Door_Within">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9499718-sharon?shelf=fantasy-high-epic">fantasy-high-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9499718-sharon?shelf=nah">nah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9499718-sharon?shelf=2020-readathons">2020-readathons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9499718-sharon?shelf=get-this-book-away-from-me">get-this-book-away-from-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906925629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17163616521190241017">Sometimes, you go to a book sale and you see hardcover books for a dollar. That's pretty exciting, right? So you might go a little crazy.<br/>And sometimes, you see a hardcover book in really good shape for a dollar and you mistake it for a different book and you get so excited that you only skim the synopsis and buy it.<br/>And sometimes, you're Jewish and you find yourself owning a book dedicated to Jesus. <br/><br/>As a general rule, I don't read Christian fiction. In fact, I usually run in the opposite directio</span>
  <span id="freeText17163616521190241017" style="display:none">Sometimes, you go to a book sale and you see hardcover books for a dollar. That's pretty exciting, right? So you might go a little crazy.<br />And sometimes, you see a hardcover book in really good shape for a dollar and you mistake it for a different book and you get so excited that you only skim the synopsis and buy it.<br />And sometimes, you're Jewish and you find yourself owning a book dedicated to Jesus. <br /><br />As a general rule, I don't read Christian fiction. In fact, I usually run in the opposite direction. But it was already in my house and I'm basically in quarantine due to COVID-19, so I figured I'd try it just to add some pages to my yearly count. <br />Honestly, I really didn't think this book was very well written. It has some really C. S. Lewis vibes but, somehow, even LESS thinly veiled Biblical references. I feel like the author read some Narnia and said, "Cool cool, but what if your story was even <i>less</i> allegorical?"<br />The Medieval style dialogue that the people in The Realm speak with is not very compelling and the humor falls very short for me. The plot also drags in the middle - it kind of loses its way after Aiden finishes his knight training. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I 100% do NOT buy Aiden's dad's sudden change of heart at the end. If someone wakes up from a coma yelling at you about weird magic alternate reality king, you're definitely going to think it's ravings and not believe them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Also, I thought the names were kind of... bad. Like, a knight named Kindle? Really? While I was reading, when I first started I misread Paragal as paralegal, so I just called him that for the rest of the book.<br />Additionally, I know there was nothing meant by it, but the reference to blue being the color of purity and blue eyes being good or "pure" made me EXTREMELY uncomfortable for some of the associations it brought up.<br /><br />All I can say is I know this review is biased, but I won't apologize for that. I am Jewish - it's not exactly the genre I'm going to pick out for myself. But even with my bias, I found the overall writing to be poor. There's more compelling both Christian fantasy and non-religious fantasy fiction out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17163616521190241017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3011731606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3011731606" />
    <a title="Dakotah Gumm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73502822-dakotah-gumm"><img alt="Dakotah Gumm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592019946p2/73502822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3011731606?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dakotah Gumm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dakotah Gumm" href="/user/show/73502822-dakotah-gumm">Dakotah Gumm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3011731606&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011731606" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12203058120836427436">Wow. As another reviewer said, that was like being hit over the head with a Bible. It's one thing to have your faith influence your writing, and another thing to rewrite the Bible as a medieval fantasy - and this was the latter. It read like a Christian renaissance festival, complete with poorly done King James Bible language. The characters couldn't seem to decide if they wanted to use "you" or "thou", and all the dialogue was stilted and awkward. And so predictable! The "big twist" wasn't a tw</span>
  <span id="freeText12203058120836427436" style="display:none">Wow. As another reviewer said, that was like being hit over the head with a Bible. It's one thing to have your faith influence your writing, and another thing to rewrite the Bible as a medieval fantasy - and this was the latter. It read like a Christian renaissance festival, complete with poorly done King James Bible language. The characters couldn't seem to decide if they wanted to use "you" or "thou", and all the dialogue was stilted and awkward. And so predictable! The "big twist" wasn't a twist at all for anyone who knows the Christian New Testament, since the traitor's name was a play on Iscariot. All the bad guys have red eyes while all the good guys have blue. The bad guys all have evil sounding names - one of them is literally Lucifer with two letters switched! This book is as subtle as a giant pink elephant stampeding through the middle of town.<br /><br />Two stars instead of one because, if nothing else, the author did have a solid understanding of Chekhov's Gun. There weren't any loose ends to wrap up (besides the foreshadowing for the next book).<br /><br />I was really excited to pick this back up, since I read it in middle school, and it inspired me to become a writer. But much as I look back on my middle school writings with embarrassment, I feel the same way about my former attitude toward this book. It was about as enjoyable as a long, dry, fire and brimstone sermon. My time would have been better spent reading or listening to an actual sermon - at least then I would know what I was getting into.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12203058120836427436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2778498086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2778498086" />

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zjB5i26Qd8AFtDhezMnjvYAZnMIEHL2s8PtsrPXvDEeia/d2O3aVLnjiIJBFpkTTQT7IjJfSybCbtjwqX9fQrw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zNlK3OavFRcbBWZqzFJ7zHTHTsf2/bwXJRvgS/HA2wuggsQhs0n3+WZTfqRFPdyiteAaiWUzyAtOVrDNW/gH4w==')})
  }
//]]>

DISCUSSION QUESTIONS INCLUDED Story Behind the Book“When my six kids’ eyes glossed over during a reading from the Bible, I paused to explain the significance of redemption to a sin-sick soul. I was rewarded with patronizing elephant nods and more blank stares. Shortly thereafter, I awoke in the middle of the night with a medieval story enveloping my mind. I wrote it down and later read it to my children. Their waning attention transformed into complete anticipation. I was amazed and disappointed. Why did it take a fictional story, not a Bible passage, to get that response? Then I realized—that is how Jesus taught! Parables are powerful! I penned the Kingdom series to help young people get excited about the supremely significant story of Jesus Christ and His mission to save mankind.” —Chuck Black<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/33508.Wayne_Thomas_Batson">About Wayne Thomas Batson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/33508.Wayne_Thomas_Batson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1597950485p3/33508.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3891611177681432395">Wayne Thomas Batson was born in Seabrook, MD in 1968. He had an adventurous childhood and adolescence that included: building forts in the woods, crabbing and crayfishing in bays, ponds, and bayous, playing lead guitar in a heavy metal band, and teaching tennis lessons at the local recreation center. He attended Gabriel DuVal Senior High School where he wrote for the school’s newspaper and literar</span>
  <span id="freeText3891611177681432395" style="display:none">Wayne Thomas Batson was born in Seabrook, MD in 1968. He had an adventurous childhood and adolescence that included: building forts in the woods, crabbing and crayfishing in bays, ponds, and bayous, playing lead guitar in a heavy metal band, and teaching tennis lessons at the local recreation center. He attended Gabriel DuVal Senior High School where he wrote for the school’s newspaper and literary magazine. He was voted “Most Talented” in his senior year, and wrote this for his Yearbook Senior Goal: “To become a published author.” Little did he know that God had even greater plans.<br /><br />Wayne Thomas Batson has spent the last thirty years teaching Reading and English to Maryland middle school students. Wayne Thomas Batson lives in Eldersburg with his extraordinary wife of 26 years. His four adult children intermittently live at home whenever their unexpected adventures lead them. <br /><br />Batson’s writing career began in 2005 with the publication of fantasy epic, The Door Within. Since then, The Door Within, The Final Storm, Isle of Swords, and Isle of Fire have all appeared on the CBA Young Adult Bestseller List, including #2 for The Final Storm Fall 2007. To date, Batson has penned or coauthored seventeen novels and has sold well over half a million copies.<br /><br />Wayne Thomas Batson gives thanks to God for the abundant life he’s been given. He continues to write for the people he cares so deeply about because he believes that, on a deep level, we all long for another world and yearn to do something important. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3891611177681432395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
